  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer6239154857532509239"><i>Librarian Note: Alternate cover edition for ISBN <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100-seraphina' rel='nofollow noopener'>9780375866562</a>.</i><br/><br/>In her <i>New York Times</i> bestselling and Morris Award-winning debut, Rachel Hartman introduces mathematical dragons in an alternative-medieval world to fantasy and science-fiction readers of all ages. <br/><br/>Four decades of peace have done little to ease the mistrust between humans and dragons in the kingdom of Goredd. F</span>
  <span id="freeText6239154857532509239" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: Alternate cover edition for ISBN <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100-seraphina" rel="nofollow noopener">9780375866562</a>.</i><br /><br />In her <i>New York Times</i> bestselling and Morris Award-winning debut, Rachel Hartman introduces mathematical dragons in an alternative-medieval world to fantasy and science-fiction readers of all ages. <br /><br />Four decades of peace have done little to ease the mistrust between humans and dragons in the kingdom of Goredd. Folding themselves into human shape, dragons attend court as ambassadors, and lend their rational, mathematical minds to universities as scholars and teachers. As the treaty's anniversary draws near, however, tensions are high.<br /><br />Seraphina Dombegh has reason to fear both sides. An unusually gifted musician, she joins the court just as a member of the royal family is murdered—in suspiciously draconian fashion. Seraphina is drawn into the investigation, partnering with the captain of the Queen's Guard, the dangerously perceptive Prince Lucian Kiggs. While they begin to uncover hints of a sinister plot to destroy the peace, Seraphina struggles to protect her own secret, the secret behind her musical gift, one so terrible that its discovery could mean her very life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6239154857532509239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/26127529-tim-poston"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442464971i/26127529._UY100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/26127529-tim-poston">Tim Poston</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Anita, "Spoilers" are a weird modern allergy. If they really spoiled a book, we could never re-read it!<br/>I read <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre'>https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a><a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Anita, "Spoilers" are a weird modern allergy. If they really spoiled a book, we could never re-read it!<br />I read <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> every few years: so many times that I can't remember not knowing that "Reader, I married him." It's always a different book, just like <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> (where she also marries him — and the story arc makes this predictable early on) because I have grown, and see the world differently.<br /><br />To say that a book can be 'spoiled' is to say it is only a plot puzzle, and not worth reading in the first place. It's like refusing to read <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/571211.The_Meaning_of_Relativity">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5...</a> because somebody has already told you that e=mc².<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_213519534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213519534" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/213519534?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213519534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1631076882853241492">What does it take to inspire someone to read a book?<br/><br/>Is it enough to give a heartfelt plea to the book's worthiness?<br/><br/>Maybe a meme? Or jazzhands? Will jazzhands convince you?<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359706i/710599.jpg' alt='Turtle meme doing jazzhands. Your mind is blown.' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>I know, a meme about jazzhands! Admit it! This is pretty damn irresistible!</i><br/><br/>Okay, well, if you're one of those strange people who would choose a convincing, well-informed review over a meme of a tiny turtle doing jazzhands then...<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359706i/710600._SY540_.jpg' alt='More jazzhands' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Are you <b>sure</b> I can't convince you with jazzhands? Maybe throw in a shuffle for you?</i><br/><br/>Seraphina is half</span>
  <span id="freeText1631076882853241492" style="display:none">What does it take to inspire someone to read a book?<br><br>Is it enough to give a heartfelt plea to the book's worthiness?<br><br>Maybe a meme? Or jazzhands? Will jazzhands convince you?<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359706i/710599.jpg" alt="Turtle meme doing jazzhands. Your mind is blown." class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I know, a meme about jazzhands! Admit it! This is pretty damn irresistible!</i><br><br>Okay, well, if you're one of those strange people who would choose a convincing, well-informed review over a meme of a tiny turtle doing jazzhands then...<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359706i/710600._SY540_.jpg" alt="More jazzhands" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Are you <b>sure</b> I can't convince you with jazzhands? Maybe throw in a shuffle for you?</i><br><br>Seraphina is half dragon, and not because her father struggles with the basic nuances of the English language.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359706i/710601.jpg" alt="I said slay, not lay!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Well, maybe a little bit...</i><br><br>In this epic fantasy by debut author, Rachel Hartman, Seraphina is an abomination who must hide her true self from everyone lest she and her father are killed for heresy. Dragons have the ability to fold themselves into human bodies and have maintained a strenuous peace with the human kingdoms. Seraphina's life is put into jeopardy when court intrigue and mystery implicates that the treaty between dragons and humans is in danger.<br><br>Hartman's novel is almost flawlessly executed. The novel, whilst long, is easily readable. Hartman doesn't rush her narrative, but neither does it seem to drag or falter. <br><br>Aside from a few brief flashback sessions, the story is carried entirely by Seraphina who may be half human and half dragon, but she is all brilliant. She is the equivalent of some kind of bear/dragon hybrid. Like, a bear/dragon hybrid that can breath fire. Yeah, that level of coolness.<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359706i/710602._SY540_.jpg" alt="Bear/dragon hybrid breathing fire" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Well, what do you know? They have a meme for that!</i><br><br>Often in novels, the female MC will profess to be extremely smart but, much to my chagrin, behave agonizingly stupidly and prove to have the mental faculties of a gnat. Seraphina is the total opposite of TSTL. She is brilliant, charming, ballsy and brave. All the while, she is also tactile, honest and fully-developed. Actually, I can not think of a single character in this book that I could argue as being two-dimensional or aggravating.<br><br>In fact, I absolutely loved the portrayal of strong female characters in this book. It was done with such grace and humanity that I found myself respecting most of the women in this book. Glisselda and the Queen were fantastic characters whom I absolutely adored.<br><br>Kiggs, as the love interest, was believable, endearing and wonderful. His character, so eccentric, so insightful and honourable, completely won me over. His relationship with Seraphina was genuine, subtle and romantic. The best thing? He wasn't any over-developed Romanticized Alpha Male! Thank goodness! He rocked it without needing to bully, oppress or corner Seraphina in any way!<br><br>The pacing is excellent for a lengthy novel. I gobbled it up and only at the very end did I feel any desire to speed things up. It is also beautifully well-written. The imagery alone was breath-takingly beautiful. The prose were polished and elegant. It was a pleasure to read. This novel was so full of emotion, beauty and poetry that I was honestly startled because I expected none of it.<br><br>I must confess that I am an acquaintance of Hartman here on GoodReads. I had grown a healthy respect for her opinions and expression, so I entered into reading Seraphina with a certain amount of skepticism and trepidation. I wonder if Hartman felt a similar trepidation when she saw that I had applied for her ARC and decided to read it! Because, let's face it, I'm not exactly known to be the most generous of reviewers. That's probably actually an understatement.<br><br>If you think that my opinion of this book has been swayed by my association with the author, then feel free to make your own mind up about it. I'm sure more reviews will be popping up soon.<br><br>But, to be honest, I didn't know what to expect when starting this novel. I've read work by friends before and had to put them aside, with embarrassment. This time is different. When Seraphina is released, I will buy this novel and treasure it. I will probably read it again and again when I need a laugh, or a romantic story or something to relax to. In fact, I loved this novel so much that I want to recommend it to everyone. I want to go get everyone I know and make them read it. This is the kind of novel that <i>deserves</i> to be published, that <i>deserves</i> to be successful. We need more of this out there. Not another trashy teen YA. This is the good shit. Right here. <br><br>So, my question is, what will it take to inspire you to read this book?<br><br><br><br><br><i>This ARC was provided to me by Random House publishers. No money or favours were exchanged.*</i><br><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.blogspot.com/2011/11/seraphina-by-rachel-hartman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335368i/694324.jpg" width="100" height="100" alt="blog link" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://soundcloud.com/katkennedy/seraphina-by-rachel-hartman" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335368i/694326.jpg" width="100" height="100" alt="audio review" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_200260127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200260127" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200260127?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=morris">morris</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2012">starred-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=6">6</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200260127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17809191348702359168">Sometimes you read a book, agree with all positive reviews of it, but it just doesn't work for you. That's the case with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_' title='Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seraphina</a> and me.<br/><br/>Whatever you've read in 5-star reviews here, on Goodreads, is all true. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_' title='Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seraphina</a> is an intelligent fantasy set in a well-realized medieval land of Goredd which is celebrating 40-year anniversary of its peace treaty with the nation of dragons. The dragons are conceived with a lot of originality. They have an ability to "fold" into human bodies (weredragons any</span>
  <span id="freeText17809191348702359168" style="display:none">Sometimes you read a book, agree with all positive reviews of it, but it just doesn't work for you. That's the case with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_" title="Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> and me.<br /><br />Whatever you've read in 5-star reviews here, on Goodreads, is all true. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_" title="Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> is an intelligent fantasy set in a well-realized medieval land of Goredd which is celebrating 40-year anniversary of its peace treaty with the nation of dragons. The dragons are conceived with a lot of originality. They have an ability to "fold" into human bodies (weredragons anyone?) and are beings of high intelligence and logic. (I saw someone on GR draw parallels with the Vulcans, and I agree, the dragons' internal conflicts about the acceptability of strong emotions are very much in tune with Spock's in the latest incarnation of Star Trek, oops, I stay corrected, EVERY incarnation of Trek.) The mystery that sets the whole story in motion is clever and wrapped up in an interesting political intrigue. As the celebration of the truce is approaching, Goredd's heir is killed and it looks like by a dragon. The main character of the novel, Seraphina is the one who is to untangle this mystery, but not without some help from Prince Lucian Kiggs, the captain of the Queen's Guard and the fiancee to Princess of the land Glisselda. This task is not easy though, as Seraphina has a secret of her own, she is a half-dragon and, by all laws of Goredd, an abomination. And, yes, as every fan of this novel says, Seraphina is a resolute, resourceful, brave heroine.<br /><br />If I am to point at any flaws, on the plot level, I don't have much to complain about. Really, besides the naming of two prominent secondary characters Orma and Okra that creates a bit of an unneeded confusion, a couple of info-dumpy conversations that should have been mixed into the narrative better, and the unclarity of why human/dragon hybrids would be in a possession of extraordinary mental powers that are foreign to humans and dragons, my only major qualm is the romance, which is a but hasty and intense within the time frame of this novel. It's kind of an odd experience when Seraphina, after just a couple of conversations with Kiggs, suddenly realizes that she is in love, and intensely and irrevocably at that. The romance becomes a tad more grating when an unexpected jealousy subplot is introduced, but this jealousy is not just silly and mostly baseless, but misdirected as well. You see, Lucian suspects that Seraphina's secret dragon uncle Orma is her lover (for no discernible reason), while the fact that Lucian himself is engaged is forgotten for almost the entirety of the novel.<br /><br />However, all these issues can be overlooked with ease, if you are enjoying the writing and Seraphina's voice. And here, unfortunately, where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_" title="Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> and I are at an impasse. It is a matter of personal taste to be sure, but I feet the novel lacked a little something to keep me engaged. A special oomph, X-factor if you will, something to carry me forward through the rather sluggish first 100 pages or so and uninteresting to me passages about music, philosophy, saints and Seraphina's mind garden. I never connected with Seraphina, who didn't, IMO have a charisma, and that was what mainly prevented me from enjoying the novel. I appreciate the quality of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_" title="Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a>, but it is not the book I would personally return to read again and again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17809191348702359168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_347121016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/347121016" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/347121016?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13160619-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=bought-2012">bought-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=favorite-girls">favorite-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=favorite-boys">favorite-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347121016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer998078766757769821">I'll admit it: <b>I was incredibly worried about this one.</b> I'm always a bit wary when an author seems nice and friendly and everybody likes them on here. I know, that seems like a stupid thing to say, but it always sits in the back of my mind that ... maybe people are giving this book five stars because they like the author. Rest assured: <b>THIS IS NOT THE CASE.</b> I mean, sure, people who liked the book probably like Hartman too, but it's not the <i>only</i> reason. <b>This book deserves its five stars; it deser</b></span>
  <span id="freeText998078766757769821" style="display:none">I'll admit it: <b>I was incredibly worried about this one.</b> I'm always a bit wary when an author seems nice and friendly and everybody likes them on here. I know, that seems like a stupid thing to say, but it always sits in the back of my mind that ... maybe people are giving this book five stars because they like the author. Rest assured: <b>THIS IS NOT THE CASE.</b> I mean, sure, people who liked the book probably like Hartman too, but it's not the <i>only</i> reason. <b>This book deserves its five stars; it deserves ALL the stars.</b> <br /><br /><b>This is definitely a meaty book.</b> There is talk of philosophy, love, art, religion, the importance of music and dance, what it means to be human (and dragon,) as well as many other themes: <i>especially</i> acceptance (being accepted and accepting oneself.) <b>I was excited to see such a smartly written book intended for young adults that wasn't dumbed-down in the least.</b> Have your dictionary ready though (this is where a Kindle is helpful) because the vocabulary used within is not for the faint of heart. I'll admit that I was a bit annoyed that some things were never fully described (Seraphina's oud only gets a description near the end) and that all of these new words were thrown out at lightning speed, but, that's epic fantasy for you. You just have to go with it and rely on the story-telling to fill in the holes.<br /><br />I'm going to completely forgive the beginning; <b>it was bumpy and disjointed and chock-full of short, declarative sentences.</b> I don't care any more. I was nit-picking and high-lighting and tsk-ing and then ... something shifted. Hartman hit her stride and things just started to flow magically and nothing could stop me from enjoying the story. <br /><br />Oh, and the characters. <b>I loved Seraphina from the start.</b> I loved how cranky and emotional she could be, how loyal and headstrong and brave and foolhardy and loving and kind she was. She's a fantastic character and one I can't wait to read more about.<br /><br /><b>And then there's Prince Lucian and Princess Glisselda.</b> I want to separate the two of them and yet I can't bring myself to. These two were the best friends and confidants Seraphina could ask for. Glisselda was bright and sparkling but never annoying or ditsy. Lucian was witty and charming but never controlling or mean. <b>Don't get me wrong, the whole book isn't super happy fun times for everyone, but the characters are incredibly multi-dimensional.</b> They laugh, they cry, they throw temper tantrums, they question and judge, and it's all wholeheartedly believable.<br /><br /><b>The side characters and villains are equally as fantastic as their main counterpart.</b> Fruit Bat, Imlann, Orma, The Earl of Apsig, even <i>Basind</i>: they all carried their own weight and breathed life into the story. It's been a long time since I've read a tale with such a fleshed-out cast.<br /><br />I could easily go on and on here, but I think you can find what you're looking for in other reviews if you haven't already figured out that I loved this book. <b>It's an excellent entry into the epic fantasy genre, and the young adult category should feel gracious that <i>Seraphina</i> appears upon its shelves, and if you're a fan of either you owe it to yourself to check this book out.</b><br /><br /><i>An ARC was provided by NetGalley - thank you.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="998078766757769821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_758950229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/758950229" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/758950229?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer758950229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10138225276974572992">Think you've read everything about dragons? Think it's a worn-out concept? Seraphina will make you think again. Our heroine of the title lives in a human kingdom that is about to celebrate forty years of a peace treaty with the draconian race, but old prejudice dies hard. When the ruler of the dragons comes to the capital to commemorate the treaty, many factions on both sides wish to sabotage the fragile peace. Hartman's dragons are fascinating. They are part Vulcan from Star Trek -- logical bei</span>
  <span id="freeText10138225276974572992" style="display:none">Think you've read everything about dragons? Think it's a worn-out concept? Seraphina will make you think again. Our heroine of the title lives in a human kingdom that is about to celebrate forty years of a peace treaty with the draconian race, but old prejudice dies hard. When the ruler of the dragons comes to the capital to commemorate the treaty, many factions on both sides wish to sabotage the fragile peace. Hartman's dragons are fascinating. They are part Vulcan from Star Trek -- logical beings who assiduously suppress their violent emotions -- and part Benedict Cumberbatch's Sherlock -- high-functioning sociopaths who can do trigonometry in their heads and tell you exactly how many people are standing in a crowd, but who don't understand the concept of music or shaking hands (or sometimes even wearing clothes). The dragons can take on human form -- saarantrai -- which only makes things more complicated. Needless to say, dragons and humans are forbidden from falling in love, which doesn't mean it never happens . . .<br /><br />A great YA fantasy with plenty of intrigue and romance and several intertwining mysteries that will keep you reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10138225276974572992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4893921141308325270">This is one of the most unique dragon books you'll ever read. (I read it twice, and it isn't even out yet!) You see, in Seraphina's world, dragons are able to take human shape--and messy, sloppy human emotions. Seraphina's father fell in love with a beautiful singer and musician, and married her, and got a surprise. Now Seraphina is the assistant to the royal music master, struggling to keep her birth a secret, and caught up in the tensions that surround the celebrations for the 40th anniversary</span>
  <span id="freeText4893921141308325270" style="display:none">This is one of the most unique dragon books you'll ever read. (I read it twice, and it isn't even out yet!) You see, in Seraphina's world, dragons are able to take human shape--and messy, sloppy human emotions. Seraphina's father fell in love with a beautiful singer and musician, and married her, and got a surprise. Now Seraphina is the assistant to the royal music master, struggling to keep her birth a secret, and caught up in the tensions that surround the celebrations for the 40th anniversary of the peace treaty between the dragons and the humans after a long and bitter war.<br /><br />You see, not all humans want to preserve the treaty. They think they can win over huge flying creatures that spout flame. And not all dragons want to preserve the treaty. This is bad news when they can take human form and go unrecognized as spies and assassins.<br /><br />Seraphina, her musician uncle Orma, Princess Glissanda (the heir and Seraphina's music student), and Prince Lucian (in charge of security for the capital) stumble across multiple plots to destroy the treaty in the wake of a prince's murder. Can they stop a new war?<br /><br />You'll have to read the book. You won't be sorry!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer351600473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7402367085073684363"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $1.99:</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B005IQZC2M/_encoding=UTF8/ref=as_li_ss_il?coliid=I3QFGFFRYHGHUF&colid=3FG93UV4RKSAZ&psc=0&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=e4b469c69f01bc486acd766a9ad9150d' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424111073i/13717488.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518004666i/25018786.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2se90Jh'>http://amzn.to/2se90Jh</a><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/02/review-seraphina-by-rachel-hartman.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The oldest of my three younger sisters loves books as much as I do, but doesn't have nearly as much time to read (b/c reasons). Fortunately, I know her well enough to keep recs to what I know she'll love, so she can make the best use of the time she <em>does</em> have, not begrudging me my surplus of time--b/c otherwise, who would weed out the mediocre books? <br/><br/>The most recent book I knew she'd love is this one, but I was</span>
  <span id="freeText7402367085073684363" style="display:none"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $1.99:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B005IQZC2M/_encoding=UTF8/ref=as_li_ss_il?coliid=I3QFGFFRYHGHUF&amp;colid=3FG93UV4RKSAZ&amp;psc=0&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=e4b469c69f01bc486acd766a9ad9150d" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424111073i/13717488.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518004666i/25018786.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2se90Jh">http://amzn.to/2se90Jh</a><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/02/review-seraphina-by-rachel-hartman.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>The oldest of my three younger sisters loves books as much as I do, but doesn't have nearly as much time to read (b/c reasons). Fortunately, I know her well enough to keep recs to what I know she'll love, so she can make the best use of the time she <em>does</em> have, not begrudging me my surplus of time--b/c otherwise, who would weed out the mediocre books? <br><br>The most recent book I knew she'd love is this one, but I was rereading it before <em>Shadow Scale</em> is released next month, and I couldn't remember if she'd already read it (b/c my memory is crap), so the day after I finished it:<br><br><strong>Me</strong>: Hey, did you ever read <em>Seraphina</em>?<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Sarah-what?<br><strong>Me</strong>: Se-ra-phin-a. It came out like 5(ish) years ago. It's about this girl who's a half-dragon--<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Ooohhh . . . I wanna be a dragon.<br><strong>Me</strong>: Half dragon.<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Or a half dragon.<br><strong>Me</strong>: Would you really want to be a dragon?<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Depends . . . Would I lay eggs or have normal babies?<br><strong>Me</strong>: Eggs if you were a dragon, babies if you were half dragon.<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Then I want to be a dragon.<br><strong>Me</strong>: o.O<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Whatever, being a dragon would be awesome. Flying around, breathing fire, hoarding treasure--<br><strong>Me</strong>: Actually, the dragon leader guy outlawed hoarding treasure, so now they hoard knowledge.<br><strong>Sister</strong>: So I get to hoard books?!<br><strong>Me</strong>: Yep.<br><strong>Sister</strong>: Could it be any more perfect?<br> <br>NO. No, it could <em>not</em>.<br><br>As I said previously, Seraphina (the MC, not the title) is a half dragon. As such, she belongs no where and to no one. Yes, there has been a tentative peace between the two races for the past fourty years, but humans are notorious for hating that which frightens them, and these dragons are rather Vulcan-like in their views on pesky emotions. <br><br>Vulcans don't marry outside of their species (unless political reasons *squints at Spock, Sr.*), and they <em>definitely</em> don't marry for love.<br><br>Neither do dragons.<br><br>And humans are so horrified by the concept that they have half a dozen Saints encouraging medieval reactions to any cross-species dalliances. BUT they're not too worried about it, b/c like that would happen anyway--<em>everyone</em> knows they should be killing the dragons (b/c dragons).<br><br>So Seraphina lives a solitary existence, in constant fear of discovery.<br><br>That sounds rather morose, doesn't it?<br><br>Without undermining the relevant points being made, I will tell you that it absolutely isn't. <br><br>In fact, it's quietly hilarious. When Seraphina begins coming into her half dragon-ness as a preteen, she begins to have seizures brought on by strange visions of even stranger creatures she's never seen before. He uncle, on the dragon (or saar) side, asks that her father hand over the reins of her education:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"To you," sneered my father. "And what will you do with her? She can't go two hours without these infernal visions giving her seizures."<br>"We could work on that, to start. We saar have techniques for taming a rebellious brain." Orma tapped his own forehead, and then tapped it again as if the sensation intrigued him.<br>Why had it never struck me how deeply peculiar he was?</i>
</blockquote><br>And once he has those reins:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>He answered even my most impudent questions. Yes, dragons could smell colors under the right circumstances. Yes, it was a terrible idea to transform into a saarantras right after eating an aurochs.</i>
</blockquote><br>AUROCHS:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423206548i/13597593.png" width="440" height="244" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423206426i/13597591.jpg" width="480" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Saarantras is a dragon's human form, so you can see why it would be a bad idea to downsize so dramatically after aurochs consumption. *snorts*<br><br>Stuff like this is also why I believe in dragons, fyi. I mean, really . . . a dragon is basically a winged dinosaur:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423309075i/13605720.jpg" width="490" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>That may or may not have breathed fire . . . not exactly a huge stretch . . . <br><br>So the plot is fantastic. What about the characters? <br><br>ALSO fantastic.<br><br>My favorite after Seraphina herself is Lars, a blond giant, a foreigner, and a fellow musician. I would love him for his (not-so-vaguely German) accent alone:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>Lars glowered defensively, as if he anticipated a scolding or a profession of love. Yes, that was it: he thought I meant to proposition him. He wore a closed expression, as if rehearsing a speech in his head, a way to let me down gently after I stripped off all my clothes. </i>Sorry, Seraphina, I dondt like<i> grausleiner </i>thet can put their voices in my headt</blockquote><br>Orma, the dragon uncle, is wonderful as well. He gradually changes from the typical rude and insensitive dragon, to a . . . <em>less</em> rude and insensitive dragon. *snickers* Both versions are highly entertaining:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m attracting small children,” Orma muttered, twisting his hat in his hands. “Shoo it away, will you?”</i>
</blockquote><br>And when he allows himself to feel the things he's so long denied, he is helpless to express them:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Who will kiss you? Who will rock you to sleep?" His voice was slow, drowsy.<br>"You never did," I said, trying to tease him. "You were more father to me than my father, but you never did that."<br>"Someone should. Someone should love you. I will bite him if he will not."</i>
</blockquote><br>And finally, the princess, who is a bizarre yet winsome, combination of oblivious and ridiculous:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Two Knights came to the castle today!" She could barely contain herself; her hands fluttered about like two excitable small birds . . . "They claim to have spotted a rogue dragon, flying around the countryside in its natural shape! Isn't that awful?"<br>Awful enough to have her grinning ear to ear. She was a strange little princess.</i>
</blockquote><br>While still somehow managing to be highly intelligent, and on occasion, even wise.<br><br>Ultimately, <em>Seraphina</em> is one of those books that never really goes away. Along with <b>
  <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/01/review-poison-study-by-maria-v-snyder.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Study</a>
</b>, it was one of the first YA fantasies that I read and loved as an adult, so once again, I was worried about whether or not it would live up to my memories . . . <br><br>I should not have been. It was every bit as clever and amusing, as pertinent and thought-provoking, and as lovely and bittersweet as I remembered. Highly recommended. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="7402367085073684363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_230323675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230323675" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230323675?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230323675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2955112844165143739">I hate it when I have the impression that I am reading a different book from other readers whose opinion I value. Hate it. But it happens and unfortunately, it happened with this book. I've read some really glowing reviews but, alas, I can't just - partially - share the love. <br/><br/>Objectively, <i>Seraphina</i> meets all the requirements to become the next epic fantasy series: it has an original take on a fairly exploited theme - dragons -, an amazing world-building, a well formed, strong main character, a 5</span>
  <span id="freeText2955112844165143739" style="display:none">I hate it when I have the impression that I am reading a different book from other readers whose opinion I value. Hate it. But it happens and unfortunately, it happened with this book. I've read some really glowing reviews but, alas, I can't just - partially - share the love. <br /><br />Objectively, <i>Seraphina</i> meets all the requirements to become the next epic fantasy series: it has an original take on a fairly exploited theme - dragons -, an amazing world-building, a well formed, strong main character, a 5-star-worthy writing style. <br /><br />But let's go in order:<br />The story is set in a world where two species exist: dragons and humans. <br />Dragons, powerful creatures, mathematical minds, able to take human form (saarantrai) to interact with people, reject all emotions as weakness, to the point of excising them from their brains. <br />Humans, constrained in their fragile bodies, fear dragons above all else and despise them, even in their human form, to the point of racial discrimination. These two species have been at war with one another for the longest of times, except for the past forty years when a rather unstable truce gave apparent peace to the world. Now it's the time to renew the peace. <br />So, dragons. And humans. <br />And then, there's Seraphina. She is the unthinkable, a half-dragon. It is imperative her identity remain a secret, but when the Prince of Goredd is found brutally murdered and all fingers point to the dragons, Seraphina becomes the unwilling protagonist of an investigation to unveil a plot that is threatening to jeopardize an already unstable peace and which will oblige her to face her most dreaded nightmare: the truth about herself. <br /><br />Sounds awesome, doesn't it?<br />Dragons that can take human form, that speak their own language (Mootya), that are organized and regulated by an Ardmagar and a council of Censors. I found it fascinating. In fact, the world-building is extremely well developed and detailed. To be honest, I haven't read that many books about dragons, and I'd say this is probably on the same level as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2986865.Eon_Dragoneye_Reborn__Eon___1_" title="Eon Dragoneye Reborn (Eon, #1) by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eon: Dragoneye Reborn</a>, as far a world-building goes. <br /><br />Seraphina is an amazing character. Caught in the middle between two worlds, neither here nor there, she has been taught to despise a part of herself, to keep it secreted. She lives a lie and will never be accepted by either worlds. She is an abomination. <br />I loved her passion for music, her witty personality, her intelligence and self-deprecating sense of humor. I loved how she grows during the story, how she comes to term with her feelings, how lies do not belong to her but have only been inculcated in her, how she is fundamentally honest. Even the love story, which could have been a potential love triangle, comes out as believable, growing and sweet. Lucian is a bit too much the perfect guy for me, too good through and through, but still very likable. I found much more interesting a whole set of bizarre side characters: Madame Okra, Abdo, Viridius, Orma, Basind. They had me laughing most of the time and were truly what MADE this book for me.<br /><br />Hartman's writing is what I'd define sophisticated and <i>recherché</i>. I had to look up a fair amount of words, my favorite probably being <i>houppelande</i>. There are no doubts about the quality of her writing and truly, there isn't much more to say about it.<br /><br />But I have to defend my 3 stars. <br />I'll sum it up in one word: pacing.<br />Despite the fantastic world-building, the amazing characters and the luscious writing, I had such a hard time getting through this book, I considered abandoning it on more than one occasion. The quantity of information to take in in the first, say, 150 pages of the book is massive and not always explained in a way to make it crystal clear. Some things are just thrown there and then explained 50 pages later. There's a whole universe of saints to digest that... really, were they necessary? And there is barely any action up until - I marked it - page 168.To be honest: too slow for me, sometimes it really could not keep my attention.<br />I had a hard time wrapping my head around Seraphina's "garden" and her grotesques, I felt the need for a bit more physical descriptions - of the Quigutl, for example - and a MAP. I really, really wanted to see a map. How is this world? Where is the Tanamoot? How many other kingdoms are there and where are they in respect to Goredd? <br /><br />So three stars. I enjoyed it because I was stubborn and kept reading and was finally rewarded in the second part but I'm not sure everybody would get through those first 100 and odd pages. Or maybe it's just me, other readers seem to adore it.<br />I'm looking forward to seeing the cover for it and I will surely pick up the sequel to this adventure with dragons, hoping that, with the infodump out of the way, I will find it a bit more fast-paced. <br /><br />Find this review and and more at <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2955112844165143739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426359993ra/14005979.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>It's not a bad book and it's well written. I just don't think high fantasy may be one of the genre's that I can really get into. <br/>Too many weird words and names. I mean Orma and Okra?<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/sqk3Ytn' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426359993i/14005980._SY540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>I tend to be a lazy reader and if I have to work for it by remembering odd words and names I get to where I just want to put the book down and grab another. <br/>My little requesting finger requested the second book in this series from Netgalley and it sounded so good </span>
  <span id="freeText16159043292982297341" style="display:none">I wanted to love this book, because..dragons!!<br><a href="http://imgur.com/Rj2BuNM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426359993ra/14005979.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>It's not a bad book and it's well written. I just don't think high fantasy may be one of the genre's that I can really get into. <br>Too many weird words and names. I mean Orma and Okra?<br><a href="http://imgur.com/sqk3Ytn" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>I tend to be a lazy reader and if I have to work for it by remembering odd words and names I get to where I just want to put the book down and grab another. <br>My little requesting finger requested the second book in this series from Netgalley and it sounded so good and the ratings for this one are through the roof...so what did I do? End up not caring much for the book. I'm sorry all you Seraphina lovers. <br>I'm shelving it for now and I may try it again later.</span>

<div id="review_250288636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/250288636" />
    <a title="Dija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2857113-dija"><img alt="Dija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360335537p2/2857113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/250288636?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dija" href="/user/show/2857113-dija">Dija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Dija by: </span>
      Buddy read with Anzu. :)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=awww">awww</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=wow">wow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=buddy-slash-group-read">buddy-slash-group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=july-2012">july-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250288636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6697239783917213058"><b>How <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina' title='Seraphina by Rachel Hartman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seraphina</a> is different from nearly all the young adult novels out there, especially of the fantasy/paranormal variety:</b><br/><br/><b>1.</b> There isn't a single moment in here where you'll want to a) throttle any of the main characters, b) stab yourself in the eye, or c) smirk at the cheesy dialogue. <br/><br/><b>2.</b> You know all those books with dragons? The ones that seem either too clichéd or too different from what <i>you</i> imagined dragons as? <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina' title='Seraphina by Rachel Hartman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seraphina</a> is about as far from those books as it gets. In fact, it's in another l</span>
  <span id="freeText6697239783917213058" style="display:none"><b>How <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina" title="Seraphina by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> is different from nearly all the young adult novels out there, especially of the fantasy/paranormal variety:</b><br /><br /><b>1.</b> There isn't a single moment in here where you'll want to a) throttle any of the main characters, b) stab yourself in the eye, or c) smirk at the cheesy dialogue. <br /><br /><b>2.</b> You know all those books with dragons? The ones that seem either too clichéd or too different from what <i>you</i> imagined dragons as? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina" title="Seraphina by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> is about as far from those books as it gets. In fact, it's in another league altogether, one where dragons are cold, manipulating creatures completely independent of humans and humans operate under the misconception that they actually have some control over the beasts.<br /><br /><b>3.</b> The world-building is exceptionally meticulous. There's no info-dumping going on here; the world is well-built and very well-executed. <br /><br /><b>4.</b> The plot is largely unpredictable. Not the type of unpredictable that is synonymous with unbelievable, but the sort where you're left completely awestruck, with a little bit of embarrassment thrown in because you didn't see that coming <i>at all</i>, even though most of the clues were perfectly visible.<br /><br /><b>5.</b> And finally, an enormous point in its favor is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina" title="Seraphina by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> can be read and enjoyed by both genders and all age groups. The plot and story is complex enough for adults to appreciate, but narrated in such a lively and entertaining voice that even 11+ year-olds should be able to grasp the content and, best of all, identify with Seraphina. <br /><br /><b>I highly recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina" title="Seraphina by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a> if most of the following applies to you:</b><br /><br /><b>1.</b> You are sick and tired of TSTL heroines who always wait on the hero to take the initiative on <i>everything</i>.<br /><b>2.</b> You loathe love triangles, especially poorly-executed ones.<br /><b>3.</b> You're constantly disappointed with all the potential in young adult novels being unexploited. <br /><b>4.</b> You love fairy tales and specifically Mulan because she never lets anyone boss her around and knows when to take matters into her own hands. <br /><b>5.</b> You often feel that cliffhangers are a cheap, albeit efficient, trick to get people to buy the sequel.<br /><br />The only problem I had with the book was that I never completely lost myself in the story and characters. The pacing was also highly irregular, being too slow at the beginning and too fast towards the end. <br /><br />That aside, Hartman has created an unforgettably beautiful world in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12394100.Seraphina" title="Seraphina by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a>, one I can't wait to visit again. While this can easily be a stand-alone novel, I'm delighted that it'll be a series instead because I'm not ready to say good-bye to Seraphina and Kiggs just yet. <br /><br /><b>Absolute favorite quote:</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["I can't bear that you'll be alone."<br />"Not alone. There are others of my kind. I'm going to find them."<br />"Who will kiss you? Who will rock you to sleep?" His voice was slow, drowsy.<br />"You never did," I said, trying to tease him. "You were more father to me than my father, but you never did that."<br />"Someone should. Someone should love you. I will bite him if he will not." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />3.5/5 stars<br /><br /><b>For more reviews, visit my <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>.</b></span>

<div id="review_226289177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226289177" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226289177?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-favs">2011-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=pure-win">pure-win</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=epic">epic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226289177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5143503582618031940"><br/><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Oh yes, Rachel Hartman. <i>YES!</i><br/><br/>This.was.good.<br/><br/>I usually don't pick up many high fantasy novels. For example, I hate Lord of the Rings. Don't flame me! It's just that it's not usually a genre I mesh well with. In fact, I think aside from <i>Seraphina</i> I have read a grand total of two high fantasy books this year: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2986865.Dragoneye_Reborn__Eon___1_' title='Dragoneye Reborn (Eon, #1) by Alison Goodman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eon: Dragoneye Reborn</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7992995.Eona_The_Last_Dragoneye__Eon___2_' title='Eona The Last Dragoneye (Eon, #2) by Alison Goodman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eona: The Last Dragoneye</a>. Coincidentally, all three have dragons in them. <s>Hmm...perhaps the universe is trying to tell me something there.</s> <br/><br/>Drago</span>
  <span id="freeText5143503582618031940" style="display:none"><br><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</b><br><br>Oh yes, Rachel Hartman. <i>YES!</i><br><br>This.was.good.<br><br>I usually don't pick up many high fantasy novels. For example, I hate Lord of the Rings. Don't flame me! It's just that it's not usually a genre I mesh well with. In fact, I think aside from <i>Seraphina</i> I have read a grand total of two high fantasy books this year: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2986865.Dragoneye_Reborn__Eon___1_" title="Dragoneye Reborn (Eon, #1) by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eon: Dragoneye Reborn</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7992995.Eona_The_Last_Dragoneye__Eon___2_" title="Eona The Last Dragoneye (Eon, #2) by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eona: The Last Dragoneye</a>. Coincidentally, all three have dragons in them. <s>Hmm...perhaps the universe is trying to tell me something there.</s> <br><br>Dragons?! Yes, <i>dragons</i>. I know what you're probably thinking. So, let me help you. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380361709ra/712756.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Who's a good boy, Toothless? I could watch him chase that little light all day. But, no, not those kinds of dragons.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361709i/712757.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Burn, baby, burn. Now, <b>that's</b> more like it.</i><br><br>Sixteen-year-old Seraphina Dombegh lives in a world where dragons have the ability to transform their bodies into humans and walk amongst mankind. Previously, dragons and humans have warred against one another, but for forty years there has been strained peace thanks to a treaty. The time arrives for the peace treaty to once again be signed and a member of the royal family has been found murdered. What's even more interesting is that it appears to be the work of a dragon. With Treaty Day swiftly approaching, Seraphina finds herself in the midst of the investigation, assisting Prince Lucian Kiggs in discovering the murderer, all the while trying desperately to hide her own secret: being half dragon.<br><br>A few things I LOVED about Seraphina:<br><br><b>The World Building:</b> <br><br>I really have to commend Hartman because this is a brilliant debut and I feel very fortunate to have read it months before the release. She has created a very believable society and I can just imagine all the research she put into this crafting the religion, clothing, races, philosophers, customs, ect. Initially, when I first started I felt a bit overwhelmed because of the names and culture. It's just that <i>rich</i>. But once I got into the story, I was just amazed at how well constructed the world building was. <br><br><b>The Characters:</b><br><br>I have to say, I was not once irritated at the main character, Seraphina (BTW: <i>awesome</i> name!). She is very headstrong and determined. When she first discovers a plot to disrupt the peace, she does not hesitate to get to the bottom of things even if that means doing things herself. This, of course, is her strength and her weakness. Having to hide her secret her whole life has left her unable to trust easily. This directly impacts her relationship with her partner in the investigation, Prince Lucian Kiggs. But as the novel wears on, we see a growth in Seraphina and her ability to trust and rely on her friends.<br><br>My favorite character has to be a toss-up between Princess Glisselda and Orma. For secondary characters, I felt they were very well developed throughout the novel. It's kind of ironic that they would come to be my favorites since in the beginning I didn't really care for either one. They possessed qualities (or at least I thought they did) that I found ugly (rudeness, apathetic, tactless, and uncaring). I suppose this is just another cool point for Hartman's writing style and character development for changing my mind completely before the novel's end. <br><br><b>The Plot and The Pacing:</b><br><br>Simply brilliant. The best way I can describe it would be to say it's like a cross between Sherlock Holmes and dragon lore fantasy. I found the novel's length to be perfect for the pacing, giving just the right amount of time for relationships to develop, the mystery to be solved, and ending realistically. <br><br><b>The Ending:</b><br><br>Very well done! I never saw the ending coming and was left completely satisfied with it. There are some series where the installments feel more like a part one or part two of a story, but then there are others like <i>Seraphina</i> that could stand alone just fine. While I know Seraphina's journey is not yet over, the immediate threat in the novel is resolved. I really appreciated that. This novel speaks for itself and doesn't need to rely on a cliffhanger to keep a reader interested in a sequel.<br><br><i>Seraphina</i> is definitely a book you should look out for in 2012. I, for one, cannot <b>wait</b> for the sequel! <br><br><i>Disclaimer: An ARC was provided by the publisher for reviewing purposes and while Rachel Hartman is a GoodReads friend of mine, these are my honest thoughts on the book.</i><br><br><i>More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</i><br><br><b>Please DO NOT click the spoilers in the comments. They are real and will ruin the book for you!</b><br></span>

<div id="review_498691321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/498691321" />
    <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater"><img alt="Maggie Stiefvater" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587234846p2/1246837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/498691321?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Stiefvater" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater">Maggie Stiefvater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer498691321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13050437163826588748">I talked about this one on NPR (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.npr.org/2012/12/22/167562764/5-young-adult-novels-that-youll-never-outgrow'>http://www.npr.org/2012/12/22/1675627...</a>) when I was highlighting the best 2012 YA fiction I'd read IN 2012. <br/><br/>Here's what I said:<br/><br/>My relationship with high fantasy — fantasy set in another world — has always been tumultuous. Actually, I'd like to refer you to the first item on this list. Everything I said about historical fiction also applies here. Which is why, despite multiple recommendations, I let this debut novel about a half-dragon, half-human girl sit unread </span>
  <span id="freeText13050437163826588748" style="display:none">I talked about this one on NPR (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.npr.org/2012/12/22/167562764/5-young-adult-novels-that-youll-never-outgrow">http://www.npr.org/2012/12/22/1675627...</a>) when I was highlighting the best 2012 YA fiction I'd read IN 2012. <br /><br />Here's what I said:<br /><br />My relationship with high fantasy — fantasy set in another world — has always been tumultuous. Actually, I'd like to refer you to the first item on this list. Everything I said about historical fiction also applies here. Which is why, despite multiple recommendations, I let this debut novel about a half-dragon, half-human girl sit unread on my desk for five months. I'll admit I very much wanted to remain a curmudgeon, but the thorough world-building and specific characters won me over. This city of austere dragons and emotional humans felt complete, as if I could turn down any number of alleys and never find the seams showing. At 480 pages, the novel is satisfyingly plump with politics, religion and prejudice — and a restrained but edifying measure of love. It also has a healthy dose of music (I was unsurprised to discover Rachel Hartman was a fellow admirer of medieval polyphony), and I find I'm very interested to see what Hartman writes next. Teens and adults alike will love to creep down the magical streets of Seraphina's city. I certainly did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13050437163826588748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
