<div id="review_229022703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229022703" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229022703?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229022703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12252040830824059194">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Fantasy lovers, rejoice!<br/><br/>This is an amazing debut novel, and I feel confident that we have a new series to devour, covet, and hoard ARCs of in a cave somewhere. Not that I do that.<br/><br/>This is the story of two societies, diametrically different, but living together under a fragile peace treaty. The dragons are analytical thinkers who don’t understand emotion, art, or music. They view emotion and attachment as distasteful and are taught strict control. But the humans are interesting to them, i</span>
  <span id="freeText12252040830824059194" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Fantasy lovers, rejoice!<br /><br />This is an amazing debut novel, and I feel confident that we have a new series to devour, covet, and hoard ARCs of in a cave somewhere. Not that I do that.<br /><br />This is the story of two societies, diametrically different, but living together under a fragile peace treaty. The dragons are analytical thinkers who don’t understand emotion, art, or music. They view emotion and attachment as distasteful and are taught strict control. But the humans are interesting to them, in an intellectual sense, and so they begin to transform themselves - to take human shape and study human behaviors. And as any two societies who live side by side, the humans and the dragons collide, damage, and change one another irrevocably. Seraphina is the product of that change: a human/dragon hybrid born from a dragon mother who found that she could love passionately and couldn’t go back. Seraphina is an abomination, and can’t reveal her true identity for fear of violent intolerance. <br /><br />This is fantasy at its absolute best: the landscape and inhabitants, customs, religion, language, and conflicts might be completely imaginary, but they are also so completely fathomable and rife with emotional honesty. Fantasy allows us to take up the role of outsider, explorer, looking in and discovering for the first time. But the amazing thing is that for all its foreignness, fantasy can gift us with so much real insight into our own society. It's as if, by acting as outsiders, we can see everything more clearly.<br /><br />That’s what I felt when I read this book. This could very well be a book about civil rights, or women’s rights, or gay rights. Seraphina is born into an identity that she didn’t choose, and must deal with the shame, the lies, and a future without true connection to anyone. And just like in our own society, there are those who view any kind of novelty or change as a threat to their very existence. <br /><br />This is a serious book, but it also made me laugh, sigh, and struggle with a lump in my throat. Seraphina is a completely inspiring heroine, beautiful in her vulnerability and naked bravery. The romance is a true meeting of the minds; I’m not sure that I even know what Lucian Kiggs really looks like. The writing is lovely (what a gorgeous opening paragraph!) and truly got under my skin in a few places. There were only a few times where I felt like a little bit <i>less</i> would have made more of an impact. But there is so much potential here; I suspect that this author will only get better.<br /><br />And I will never, ever underestimate the seductive power of math.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Bjork – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VDSJjeUhJf0" rel="nofollow noopener">Joga</a><br /><br />I kept returning to Bjork while reading this. Her new album is (like her others) highly experimental. She uses uncommon musical structure and even some brand new instruments that she’s invented. The album comes with a downloadable app so that listeners can “interact with” the music. After reading this book, I can only conclude that Bjork is a human-dragon hybrid.<br /> <br />This is one of my favorites of hers, and I think that the lyrics and the mood can relate so heavily to the dragons, in human form, and experiencing strong emotions that they can’t decipher.<br /><br /><i>”You don't have to speak<br />I feel<br />Emotional landscapes<br />They puzzle me<br />Confuse<br /><br />Then the riddle gets solved and you push me up to this<br />State of emergency<br />How beautiful to be”</i><br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/07/ya-review-seraphina-by-rachel-hartman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12252040830824059194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_232310391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232310391" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232310391?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=hmm-that-was-interesting">hmm-that-was-interesting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=i-ll-stalk-you-til-you-read-it">i-ll-stalk-you-til-you-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=speshul-snowflake">speshul-snowflake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=wrung-me-dry">wrung-me-dry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-loved">books-i-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232310391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13373858129155825218">You know, the internet is a strange place. You meet so many people, and they influence your life in so many ways, and yet you might spend an entire lifetime without ever once seeing the face of the person you count as a friend. And yet, they <i>are</i> friends. Maybe not the kind you can call at one in the night to cry about your cheating asshole of a boyfriend, but the kind you'd like to meet for a drink, and chill out with and have fun, stimulating conversation with. <br/><br/>And so, with prolonged internet i</span>
  <span id="freeText13373858129155825218" style="display:none">You know, the internet is a strange place. You meet so many people, and they influence your life in so many ways, and yet you might spend an entire lifetime without ever once seeing the face of the person you count as a friend. And yet, they <i>are</i> friends. Maybe not the kind you can call at one in the night to cry about your cheating asshole of a boyfriend, but the kind you'd like to meet for a drink, and chill out with and have fun, stimulating conversation with. <br><br>And so, with prolonged internet interaction comes this weird feeling of <i>knowing</i> someone. I think this may be even more true of people on Goodreads, because I feel like we put so much of ourselves into our reviews, and then we just send it out there for the world to see. Little bits and pieces of our souls, just floating around on the interwebs. <br><br>So, to get to the point (and yes, there <i>was</i> a point in there. Somewhere.) I've been 'friends' with Rachel Hartman for a while now. And I adore her to bits. She's smart and she's freakin' <i>
  <b>hilarious</b>
</i> and she's talented. So talented, she can draw pictures in your mind with one sentence. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And no, she's not paying me to say this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And no, I'm not sleeping with her either. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But despite the friendship and the internet-based intimacy et al, Seraphina took me completely, totally by surprise. Not in its awesomeness, because awesomeness was pretty much guaranteed, but in the method of its awesome. <br><br>I was expecting this book to be witty and self-deprecating and obscurely erudite. And it <i>was</i> all those things. But it was also sharply poignant and touching and introspective. It was a book about dragons, and dragons are made of win, of course; but it was also a book about growing up and finding yourself and <i>accepting</i> yourself. It was a book about how no (wo)man is an island, and it was a book about how Shrek thought Fiona was so much more beautiful as an ogress. It was a tribute to the beauty of being flawed, and it was a tribute to the age of honorable men. <br><br>This book takes the serious, makes it absurd and then makes you think beyond the absurdity. Look into the heart of things, and Fruit Bat will become more than just a cute nickname. Seraphina is the heart of this book, but its in the supporting cast that the book finds its soul. Little bits of soul, floating through the pages. Almost like real life.<br><br>And Uncle Orma. Uncle Orma was my absolute favorite. How could I help it?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362674ra/713858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>It's Spock with scales!!!</i><br><br>And Kiggs. Kiggs was so awesome. A man in a million, with his honor intact, and so beautifully human and flawed. Screw you, alpha males, a <i>real</i> man gets angry, gets scared, gets stupid. They can't all be (insert standard Twilight insult/reference here) perfect sparkling marble sculptures! <br><br>And, saving the best for last, Seraphina was ADORABLE. She's all the things I want my characters to be. Smart? Check. Believable? Check. Real-as-all-hell? Check. Annoying and amazing in turns? Check. Pay attention, you YA writers, <i>this</i> is how it's done!<br><br>The only thing that drove me nuts about this book was a little conceit that was so peculiarly Rachel, I couldn't help but forgive her for it. The story is full of (totally made-up) references to random philosophers, a shared point between Kiggs and Seraphina, sure, but one that totally excludes the reader. The characters talk about these philosophers and their philosophies like we've already read all of their writings and are just coming into the middle of a perfectly-comprehensible debate about them, but the truth of the matter is, you're mostly left scratching your head and wondering what the eff they're going on about. It felt like Rachel was trying so hard to make sure the connection between her characters was as much intellectual as emotional, that she went a bit overboard with it all. <br><br>But. BUT. This book will rock your socks off, if you have any interest at all in interesting, well-written fantasy. It's not the fast-and-easy kind of read; rather, it is full of the unsaid and the unwritten, things that you have to <i>think</i> about, ideas that you have to process, emotions that you have to absorb. But in the end, so completely, totally worth it in a way I can't even begin to express. <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13373858129155825218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=bitchin-female-protagonist">bitchin-female-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1854646358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10184518177302327174"><i>
  <b>“We were all monsters and bastards, and we were all beautiful.”</b>
</i> <br/><br/>This book deserves all the stars. <br/><br/>I loved it. Loved it. <br/><br/>Beautiful message, sophisticated plotting, sweet and believable romance, awesome main character who managed to be both ordinary and believable while also being the "brave hero". <br/><br/>Read in one 7 hour sitting.<br/><br/><i>So what was so wonderful about this book?</i><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“The world inside myself is vaster and richer than this paltry plane, peopled with mere galaxies and gods.”</b>
</i> <br/><br/><b>Seraphina</b> addresse</span>
  <span id="freeText10184518177302327174" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“We were all monsters and bastards, and we were all beautiful.”</b>
</i> <br /><br />This book deserves all the stars. <br /><br />I loved it. Loved it. <br /><br />Beautiful message, sophisticated plotting, sweet and believable romance, awesome main character who managed to be both ordinary and believable while also being the "brave hero". <br /><br />Read in one 7 hour sitting.<br /><br /><i>So what was so wonderful about this book?</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“The world inside myself is vaster and richer than this paltry plane, peopled with mere galaxies and gods.”</b>
</i> <br /><br /><b>Seraphina</b> addresses self acceptance in a way that felt relatable. Self acceptance is a BIG DEAL in the YA genre. In fact, self hatred and an obsessive fear of social rejection is pretty much how you know you are reading <i>another bloody YA book</i>. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I barely noticed loneliness anymore; it was my normal condition, by necessity if not by nature.”</b>
</i> <br /><br />But it is handled so well in this novel! A social system is built into the world of the novel where Serephina's fear makes sense. The plot question isn't "will she get validation thru the hot love interest, finally proving how hot and cool she is". The plot question becomes- will Serephina survive a dangerous situation in which her body, <i>her basic genetics</i>, could betray her. <br /><br />And this is nicely balanced with faith in herself. She has real skills which she has honed over years of practice. She isn't falsely modest about her strengths. But she is deeply afraid of connection and the complicated dangers of risking exposing herself. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“That’s the secret to performance: conviction. The right note played tentatively still misses its mark, but play boldly and no one will question you. If one believes there is truth in art – and I do – then it’s troubling how similar the skill of performing is to lying. Maybe lying is itself a kind of art. I think about that more than I should.”</b>
</i><br /><br />As a result, the novel perfectly melds this cliched theme with believable setting and character. I'm not ashamed to say I had a lump in my throat when Hartman resolved this thematic arc. It was incredibly poignant. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Love is not a disease...I cannot let them cut you out of me, nor her either. I will cling to my sickness, if it is a sickness. I will hold it close to me like the sun.”</b>
</i><br /><br />The novel explores intimacy and isolation, dishonesty and truth-telling and how we all grapple with our own prejudices. It surprised me. The book managed to be both a familiar story and a surprisingly deep exploration of self- understanding. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I felt lighter when I had finished, and for once emptiness was a sweet relief and a condition to be treasured.” </b>
</i> <br /><br />It is heavy on politics, and for readers unfamiliar with the genre it is perhaps a steep learning curve, but regular fantasy readers will enjoy the well thought out world and stunning, evocative language. <br /><br />It is rare these days for me to feel a lot of emotion about a book, I don't know- maybe I read too many… if such a thing is even possible. But often I see the author's hand behind the story and I say to myself, "yes very well done, I can see what emotion you are evoking here"… but I don't really feel it- like <b>kick in the gut</b> feel it. <br /><br />I did with this one. And even better- even with all this heavy shit going on I laughed. The dialogue is witty, the commentary has this very dry, amusing tone. <br /><br />Again this book surprises by managing to pack an emotional punch while also knowing what it is- a light hearted fantasy about dragons. <br /><br />Recommended for: anyone who enjoys more cerebral fantasy (it is heavy on diplomacy and light on sword and sorcery), people looking for wholesome story telling that isn't fluffy, and anyone for a hard on for dragons of the Temeraire style (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28876.His_Majesty_s_Dragon__Temeraire___1_" title="His Majesty's Dragon (Temeraire, #1) by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">His Majesty's Dragon</a>).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10184518177302327174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_441452059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441452059" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441452059?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441452059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17940913799994826012">I have so much love for Rachel Hartman and this book! My five-star ratings are few and far between, but I’d give Seraphina ten if I could. It was so easy to get lost in this world of humans, dragons and those in-between – I still haven’t found my way back. <br/><br/>Hartman’s dragons are magnificent creatures, full of intersting paradoxes. On a physical level, they produce fire, but on an emotional level, they’re cold and tightly controlled. They go to great lengths to remain emotionless, even though thei</span>
  <span id="freeText17940913799994826012" style="display:none">I have so much love for Rachel Hartman and this book! My five-star ratings are few and far between, but I’d give Seraphina ten if I could. It was so easy to get lost in this world of humans, dragons and those in-between – I still haven’t found my way back. <br><br>Hartman’s dragons are magnificent creatures, full of intersting paradoxes. On a physical level, they produce fire, but on an emotional level, they’re cold and tightly controlled. They go to great lengths to remain emotionless, even though their <i>saars</i> (human shapes) are more susceptible to emotions. They have ways to excise these unwanted emotions from their brains and they keep close watch on dragons suspected of harboring human emotions. <br><br><b>
  <i>Dragons used meditation and what Orma called cognitive architecture to partition their minds into discrete spaces. They kept their maternal memories in one room, for example, because they were disruptively intense; the one maternal memory I’d experienced had bowled me over. Emotions, which the saar found uncomfortable and overpowering, were locked away securely and never permitted to leak out.</i>
</b><br><br>The world Hartman created has a distinctly Medieval feel, but with many exceptions and liberties that were quite unimaginable in the Middle Ages. She took the time to build this world, which resulted in somewhat slower pacing, but I didn’t mind in the least. I find that I’m willing to suffer through almost anything if that means I’ll end up with a complete and well thought-out world. Fortunately, Hartman’s intricate worldbuilding didn’t come at a price. From the very first sentence, Seraphina had me entranced. I took my time reading it and I appreciate that it allowed me to do that. The best books aren’t those that practically force you to turn pages. True works of art permit you to enjoy them slowly, at your own pace, and it takes a great author to achieve that.<br><br><br>As for Seraphina, oh my! If there was ever a heroine one could admire with no doubts or hesitations, a heroine whose every action is an inspiration, it’s Maid Seraphina Dombegh. Half-human and half-dragon, she isn’t even supposed to exist, and yet she finds a way to live so fully despite her need for secrecy. Phina has the best of both worlds: quick logical thinking and problem solving typical of dragons tempered with inherently human warmth and loyalty. I think these words directed to her by Dame Okra, another half-dragon, describe her better than I ever could:<br><br><b>
  <i>Whatever else may be true of you, you do things your own way, with a refreshingly self-assured pigheadedness. I like that!</i>
</b> <br><br>Over time, Seraphina falls deeply in love with Prince Lucian Kiggs, queen’s bastard grandson and fiancé of Princess Glisselda, heir to the throne. Kiggs is the captain of the Queen’s Guard, competent, fiercely intelligent, and loyal to a fault. When she first meets him, Seraphina thinks of him as plain, but the more time she spends with him, the more beautiful he becomes in her eyes. They share so much, these two – their curiosity and love for philosophy, but above all, their loyalty to Glisselda, which makes it impossible for them to be together. Such bittersweet, well-written romance would be my favorite part in any book, but in Seraphina, the competition is hard. Singling anything out would be unfair to all the other parts I absolutely adore. <br><br>As soon as Dracomachia gets a cover, I’ll pre-order a copy. I don’t pre-order books with no covers, it’s just another one of my oddities, but this one almost made me break my own rule. <br><br>I hope my friend Catie will forgive me for stealing her line, but I simply couldn’t resist:<br>Fantasy lovers, rejoice! <br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17940913799994826012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1828415812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1828415812" />
    <a title="Argona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/349639-argona"><img alt="Argona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476301474p2/349639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1828415812?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Argona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Argona" href="/user/show/349639-argona">Argona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=medieval-fantasy">medieval-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=royals">royals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=favorite-fantasy-series">favorite-fantasy-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1828415812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10110565635808628822">Buddy read with my dear friend, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12222982-roya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roya</a>! You can read her wonderful review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212001878?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>As a fan of High fantasy and dragons, I really enjoyed reading this book. Like most High fantasy books, the beginning is rather slow but it’s well executed and didn’t drag or bore me to death. The setting of this medieval world is well-developed and interesting. Both humans and dragons have their own histories and way of thinking. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481826270i/21459629._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love dragons and Hartman’s version of dragons as a species capable of shifting into huma</span>
  <span id="freeText10110565635808628822" style="display:none">Buddy read with my dear friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12222982-roya" rel="nofollow noopener">Roya</a>! You can read her wonderful review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212001878?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br><br>As a fan of High fantasy and dragons, I really enjoyed reading this book. Like most High fantasy books, the beginning is rather slow but it’s well executed and didn’t drag or bore me to death. The setting of this medieval world is well-developed and interesting. Both humans and dragons have their own histories and way of thinking. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481826270i/21459629._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love dragons and Hartman’s version of dragons as a species capable of shifting into human form is quite well-thought and original. They are highly intelligent and are rather similar to “Vulcan” species from “Star Trek”, especially when it comes to their way of thinking, their social interactions or their internal emotional conflicts. They love science, especially math, and follow logic. They find emotions destructive and have trouble understanding it. They believe in a concept called “Ard”, an ethical and physical rightness imposed on the chaos of the world, which they use to organize their memories and thoughts or even lock away emotions. Once they used to hoard gold, but after their truce with humans, many of them have come to hoard books, which is their way of hoarding science. Adorable!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455881271i/18162650._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Most of the story takes place in the human city of Goredd. Goredd is governed by monarchy, queens in particular, and people are quite religious. Hartman has actually developed a religion for her story, with quite a number of saints that are assigned to infants as patrons, some of which have very entertaining or creepy descriptions. I found it quite curious that humans in this book were so afraid of oddities or anything they might find abnormal and yet, they worshiped such bizarre saints. I can't help but wonder if there is something behind the whole thing.<br><br>I found Seraphina's character peculiar and adorable. She is grumpy and reclusive, avoiding contact with others as much as possible and preferring her own isolated space. There is a reason for this and her true character, hidden under the insecurities, is revealed as the story develops. She is also geeky, in love with science, music, math and intellectual pursuit. She is constantly facing internal conflict, a conflict that sometimes takes a magical form or hits her in the form of visions. Hartman uses imagery to describe both complex emotions and music, and in my opinion, captures the essence of both successfully.<br><br>As a female character, she was actually strong and smart, loyal and brave. She didn’t annoy me and did not make me think of different ways of murdering her, which is really something. Many female characters manage to awaken my dark side and the desire to off them in painful ways. I think this book actually succeeds in portraying strong female characters, something that many authors try to achieve but fail spectacularly.<br><br>The romance was perfect for me. I don’t like instant love. Seraphina’s relationship with her love interest develops gradually and in a meaningful way, with very good chemistry between them. The story did not focus on him at the beginning, and he was not described in details, making it obvious that he is indeed The One.<br><br>The relationship develops as the characters are forced to interact, forced since Seraphina tries to socialize as little as possible. The two of them have much in common and actually spend time discovering each other, pulling out the layers one by one. HE is eccentric, open-minded, insightful, and just as geeky as Seraphina, with his own adorable peculiarities.<br><br>Most of the other characters of the book were also well-developed and memorable, with depth, background and unique personalities of their own. They acted realistic and I wasn’t rolling my eyes through most of the story, wondering why the stupid characters didn’t see what was right in front of them.<br><br>Orma, Seraphina’s uncle, was specially my favorite and I found him very entertaining and adorable. He has his own inner conflicts and his transformation from a cold and insensitive uncle to a loving, caring and protective one was quite beautiful and lovely.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481827128i/21459745._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The plot was quite engaging and well-thought. But I think this book is not merely about a mystery that surrounds a certain death and finding the murderer. It is actually about coming to terms with one’s identity and embracing it. It is about facing an unfair world, cruelty of your own people, prejudice and racism. It’s about standing up for yourself, finding a purpose for your life and trying to change the world around you for the better. It's about finding freedom and love.<br> <br>I am not saying this book is perfect. There were some changes of heart that felt a little rushed. There were also a few things that were left unexplained, probably to explore in the second book. This book does not end in a cliffhanger but the story is clearly unfinished. The ending is realistic and bittersweet, leaving the reader with hope for a better future. <br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed this book. I think Seraphina is a fantastic, thought-provoking fantasy. I believe I actually gained more than entertainment by reading this book and that it managed to affect me in a positive way.<br><br>“We were all monsters and bastards, and we were all beautiful.”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481825433i/21459534._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10110565635808628822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_225646440" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225646440" />
    <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-"><img alt="Jillian -always aspiring-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393566262p2/3085436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225646440?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian -always aspiring-" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who enjoy fantasy that never forgets the importance of emotion and characterization</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=heroines-i-love-and-or-admire">heroines-i-love-and-or-admire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wowed-me">wowed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-endings">best-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-couples">best-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=ultimate-favorites">ultimate-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=forewent-sleep-to-read-it">forewent-sleep-to-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wish-i-could-write-a-book-like-this">wish-i-could-write-a-book-like-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=writing-to-which-i-aspire">writing-to-which-i-aspire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225646440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9586240909732502631">Fantasy is my favorite genre, but oftentimes I find that fantasy tales are often too simplistic or too pretentious for my liking. Fantasy authors have the burdensome task of creating worlds and cultures that <i>feel</i> real and somewhat familiar but nonetheless offer a sense of danger, wonder, and excitement that few of us experience in our day-to-day lives. In the end, many fantasy novels don't sustain that balance of normalcy and humanity interwoven with the threads of fantasy...but <i>Seraphina</i> remark</span>
  <span id="freeText9586240909732502631" style="display:none">Fantasy is my favorite genre, but oftentimes I find that fantasy tales are often too simplistic or too pretentious for my liking. Fantasy authors have the burdensome task of creating worlds and cultures that <i>feel</i> real and somewhat familiar but nonetheless offer a sense of danger, wonder, and excitement that few of us experience in our day-to-day lives. In the end, many fantasy novels don't sustain that balance of normalcy and humanity interwoven with the threads of fantasy...but <i>Seraphina</i> remarkably did.<br /><br /><i>Seraphina</i> is a tale of dragons and intrigues, music and emotions, humanity and prejudices. Forty years prior, the age of knights battling dragons ended with a peace treaty between the queen of Goredd and the king of dragons. Now, dragons shift into human skins and live among humans...but the animosity between the two kinds is far from forgotten. Seraphina Dombegh copes with this world and keeps to her music even as she tries her best not to be noticed, for the dragons aren't the only ones with secrets to keep...<br /><br />In the vein of novels from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13677.Gail_Carson_Levine" title="Gail Carson Levine" rel="nofollow noopener">Gail Carson Levine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce" title="Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Tamora Pierce</a>, the kind of fantasy represented here sings of both our world and another world quite different from our own. Religion here acts as either a comfort or simply tradition to the people who receive patron saints at their christening ceremonies; analytical minds respect studies and knowledge but have much to learn as far as the study of the heart goes; and bigotry leaks into actions due to lack of understanding and an overabundance of fear. Goredd is a well-realized fantasy world comprised of many flaws from our own societies yet many of the same fascinations as well; it's not hard to fall into the imagining that perhaps this place exists in another space and time.<br /><br />Strong and believable world-building aside, the novel's finest strength lies in its namesake heroine, who ties the themes and emotions running throughout the novel all together within her own existence and journey. Seraphina is by no means perfect or "too good for her own good": she has flaws and makes (sometimes mortifying) mistakes. But she isn't the kind of character who remains stagnant or oblivious to her own shortcomings. Rather, she learns from them and grows because of her experiences. If anything, more heroines should be like Seraphina, whose growth over the course of the novel is anything but superficial.<br /><br />Last but not least, the story is honestly <i>enjoyable</i>. It's not the kind of fantasy where you feel like a mere observer but rather an unseen companion to all the goings-on within Goredd. There are moments ripe for smiles and laughs, for surprise and gasps, for melancholy expressions and contemplation...and all of it is done in a straightforward yet thoughtful narrative that can't help but play with your heartstrings. <i>Seraphina</i> was all that for me and more, and I hope other readers will find treasures of thought within its pages just as I did.<br /><br />I must offer fair warning, however: the ending is bittersweet in its own way...but mostly for the fact that, with <i>Seraphina</i>'s release date of spring 2012, the wait for the sequel will be long indeed.<br /><br /><i>Note: I received an advanced copy of this book from the publisher through NetGalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9586240909732502631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_239049513" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239049513" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239049513?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239049513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1967589491735514701"><i>Review contains the slightest of slight spoilers...</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Scattered and peculiar- some of us were sceptical and bitter- we were a people. And I was at the hub of this enormous wheel. I could bring us together. In a way, I already had.”<br/></i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>I liked it better than I thought I would, which says a lot for a fantasy-phobe like me. <br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>Seraphina. The world- It was beautifully constructed. Dragons. ORMA. Courts. Concerts. Parades. Emotions. Scales. Dreams. “Tending the gard</span>
  <span id="freeText1967589491735514701" style="display:none"><i>Review contains the slightest of slight spoilers...</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Scattered and peculiar- some of us were sceptical and bitter- we were a people. And I was at the hub of this enormous wheel. I could bring us together. In a way, I already had.”<br /></i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />I liked it better than I thought I would, which says a lot for a fantasy-phobe like me. <br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />Seraphina. The world- It was beautifully constructed. Dragons. ORMA. Courts. Concerts. Parades. Emotions. Scales. Dreams. “Tending the garden” . Fruit bat. Mrs Fusspots. Gavotting. Intrigue. War. Gold. Trinkets. Secrets. Knights. Jongleurs. Memories. <br /><br /><b>Low Points.</b><br />See love interest.<br />Also, there were huge chunks of the story where hardly anything happened. I found myself flicking back to see if I’d just missed a major battle scene or something.<br />But I hadn’t. <br />When things happened it was great but, unfortunately, these parts were few and far between. <br />It’s clear that Ms Hartman is extremely skilled in world building and wow, what a world she built. It was so dense and intricate that you could imagine walking through the town. I just wish she had used some of those writing skills to add a bit more plot.<br />Now, I’m not the biggest fantasy fan (I’ve never even got through LOTR films. I know, I know. Smite me down, fantasy fans!) and I don’t mind admitting that it’s probably because of a mix of not finding it interesting and not understanding it.<br />I found Seraphina interesting and I probably understood <i>most</i> of it but I just really wanted more to happen. <br /><br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />Strong. Resourceful. Passionate. Loyal. Determined. Not whingey. <br />I loved Seraphina, she’s my kind of heroine. <br /><br />Minor blips when boys are around but I can let her off in exchange for moisturising tips. <br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />My dislike for poor Lucian Kiggs is all my own fault.<br />Because I’m silly and I kept calling him Lucian Griggs as if he was some kind of cousin that Jonah just never talked about. <br />And then I was like… no, Jo, it’s Kiggs, <i>Kiggs</i>.<br />So naturally I started calling him Lucian Giggs, like he was some kind of cousin that Ryan just never talked about. <br />(Him being Ryan Giggs’ cousin would make more sense because Mr Giggs (not Kiggs) is Welsh and everyone knows that’s where 83% of the world’s population of dragons dwell.)<br />But his name aside, I wasn’t sold with either him or Seraphina’s attraction to him. <br />I didn’t think there would be a love story in this book so I was kind of put off by the fact that there was. I had gotten it into my mind that it was going to be all about Seraphina being brilliant on every page. I would have been quite happy for it to just have been left out <i>or</i> even better, developed more slowly so we had an idea why the two of them liked each other at all. <br />I just didn’t believe in it.<br />I’m sorry, I really tried, but I just couldn’t.<br />As a fun note: You should have seen the other love interests Flann and I were inflicting on poor Seraphina throughout our readalong. <br /><br /><b>Orma</b><br />Oh mate, I loved this guy. Although I know he’d probably give me a cold look if I told him that or stab me in the side if I tried to hug him.<br />But that’s fine, because that’s why I loved him.<br />He was so hilarious and he came out with some absolutely stellar one liners (I highlighted them all but my favourite was “I’m attracting small children, shoo it away won’t you?”) and he’s the epitome of emotionally unavailable man.<br />And who doesn’t love an emotionally unavailable man?!<br />Bravo, Ms Hartman, for creating such a fantastic and interesting character.<br />Now for your next trick: <i>make him real</i>.<br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br />My favourite part of this whole book was Seraphina’s struggle with her identity and how she was supposed to fit into a society where everyone thought she was a monster.<br />I know that most people reading this book won’t know what it’s like to be a half-dragon and the emotions involved in <i>that</i>, but I truly feel a lot of people reading it will be able to relate to Seraphina’s battle to come to terms with herself and how to fit in when she was so different. <br />Ms Hartman perfectly depicted these emotions in a raw and harrowing way that will undoubtedly have a lot of resonance with a lot of readers. <br /><br />So with the explanation out of the way, this song is for Seraphina. <br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/embed/t0ko4cjin78" rel="nofollow noopener">Rootless by Marina and the Diamonds.</a><br /><br /><b>Sadness Scale.</b><br />7/10. As I mentioned in the Theme Tune section, Seraphina’s emotions and trying to fit into <i>either</i> world were extremely well-written and extremely affective. <br />Also, quick mention because I’m tiptoeing around spoilers as I would a dragon’s lair, I loved every conversation between Seraphina and Orma. They made me so happy and ache with sadness at the same time. <br />Did I mention I liked Orma?<br />Do I need to write Part 2 of my love for Orma?<br /><br />….<br /><br />No?<br />Spoilsports. <br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who like epic fantasy books. People who appreciate brilliant world-building. People who like strong heroines. People who think that dragons are misunderstood. People who wonder whether Jonah Griggs has any cousins. People who love Orma.<br /><br /><br /><i>I received an advanced copy of this book from the publisher.</i><br /><br />You can read this review and lots of other exciting things on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1967589491735514701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229484007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229484007" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319666686p2/4222084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229484007?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=debut-novels">debut-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229484007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7823769689596701499">I can count on one hand the number of fantasy books I've enjoyed, but after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213519534' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kat Kennedy's glowing review</a> of <i>Seraphina</i>, I was intrigued by the promise of smart heroines, dragons, and jazz hands. Really, who can turn down jazz hands? <br/><br/>With that in mind, I eagerly started this book. Then I got to mentions of <i>saarantrai</i>, houppelande, and <i>quigutl</i>.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362218ra/713378.gif' width='350' height='197' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Remember, amateur fantasy reader here. I'm not ashamed to admit that I'm scared off by double letters and words that start with Q.<br/><br/>Another thing that'</span>
  <span id="freeText7823769689596701499" style="display:none">I can count on one hand the number of fantasy books I've enjoyed, but after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213519534" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat Kennedy's glowing review</a> of <i>Seraphina</i>, I was intrigued by the promise of smart heroines, dragons, and jazz hands. Really, who can turn down jazz hands? <br><br>With that in mind, I eagerly started this book. Then I got to mentions of <i>saarantrai</i>, houppelande, and <i>quigutl</i>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362218ra/713378.gif" width="350" height="197" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Remember, amateur fantasy reader here. I'm not ashamed to admit that I'm scared off by double letters and words that start with Q.<br><br>Another thing that's kept me away from fantasy: the world building. I get that it's a necessary <s>evil</s> part of the genre, but... a pain in the ass to read -- especially since I am not a skimmer and I re-read things I don't understand. Quigutl? Yeah, I had to go back for that, only to find out that it wouldn't be explained til 50 pages later. <br><br>The story is a lot to take in at first because you're hit with the worlds of Goredd (human) and Tanamoot (dragon), and the half-human/half-dragon world of Seraphina. Seraphina's world is as fascinating as it is confusing because it exists in her mind, created by memories left by her deceased mother. It's populated by odd characters that Seraphina names Fruit Bat, Pelican Man, etc.<br><br>I gave myself 100 pages to decide whether to keep reading this book or not. I'm <i>so</i> glad I stuck with it.<br><br>Rachel Hartman takes what could easily be cliche characters and plot and makes them compelling and intelligent. She doesn't dumb it down for her readers or make it easy for her characters. Princess Glisselda, the fiancee of Prince Lucian, is also one of the most likable characters in the book. Prince Lucian is an actual knight in shining armor, but Seraphina is more often than not coming to <i>his</i> rescue. That brings us to Seraphina, a brilliant musician who struggles with the legacy her mother left her. I'd be pissed about metallic silver scales too.<br><br>But who has time to dwell on scales when Lucian and Glisselda's uncle has been killed and all clues (namely, the lack of a head along with the body) point to a dragon as the culprit. This murder just before the anniversary of the peace treaty between humans and dragons could tip the balance towards war. There's discontent on all sides -- humans who aren't happy living with dragons, dragons who feel they've given up too much to humans, knights who fought during the wars and were banished following the peace treaty. Assassinations are plotted and identities are revealed as the nation of Goredd plans to welcome the leader of dragonkind.<br><br>And this is just the beginning (I hope!) of a series. I don't mean to keep using the word "intelligent" but Rachel Hartman writes characters that actually use their brains. Deductive reasoning! It happens! <i>Seraphina</i> reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> in that as good as it was, I know the sequel is going to be even better. Nevertheless, this book stands very capably on its own. It is as much political thriller as it is fantasy, which I love. I also loved the discussions of parentage and the legacies, both beneficial and detrimental, that parents leave their kids. I can't believe this was a debut novel! It was so assured and entertaining. I definitely look forward to reading more of Rachel Hartman's work.<br><br><br><i>Noelle and I review this book on <a href="http://youngadultanonymous.blogspot.com/2012/07/review-seraphina-by-rachel-hartman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Anonymous</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7823769689596701499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12085736681840646212">An unsolicited Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review. Quotes have been pulled from an ARC and may be subject to change.<br/><br/>Seraphina is a half human, half dragon sixteen year old who lived in Goreddia. Humans must show their dragon counterparts that they’re superior so they tend to dominate over their scaley friends. The war has ceased, brought on by the Queen with a treaty. The Ardmagar makes the decisions for these dragons, and is basically in charge.<br/><br/>Seraphina has these gro</span>
  <span id="freeText12085736681840646212" style="display:none">An unsolicited Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher for review. Quotes have been pulled from an ARC and may be subject to change.<br /><br />Seraphina is a half human, half dragon sixteen year old who lived in Goreddia. Humans must show their dragon counterparts that they’re superior so they tend to dominate over their scaley friends. The war has ceased, brought on by the Queen with a treaty. The Ardmagar makes the decisions for these dragons, and is basically in charge.<br /><br />Seraphina has these grotesque visions that haunt her, which she aptly give nicknames to. (I had an affinity to Fruit Bat!) As for the wonderful secondary characters I liked Glisselda immensely. Kind and friendly she always defended Seraphina and was loyal to her as any sister. Lucian Kiggs, Captain of the guard was just as wonderful. Good through and through, he did the moral thing in a world where deception was the norm. His friendship with Phina was cute and sweet, and you can tell why she likes him so much.<br /><br />In a novel, where world building is done well, and there are so many characters to keep track of, a list of character’s and who they are is extremely helpful. I took lots of time trying to memorize some characters names so I didn’t have to check it. Do I think dragons can be the next trend? Well maybe. It’s been trending for a long time and Seraphina’s dragons are the ferocious and vicious ones nightmares are made of. And I for one can’t wait until book two comes out so I can join her on her adventure.<br /><br />Beautifully written, <em>Seraphina</em> will whisk you away to a world where dragons are as ferocious as anyone thought they could be.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6235359174965912563">4.5 rounded up - crazy well written.<br/><br/>Seraphina deserves every YA award for which it was nominated. The core objective of the book is to teach young ladies to accept their minds and bodies and grow into natural self-confidence. <br/>Seraphina, the heroine of the story, undergoes a huge amount of character development in learning to love herself. She goes from:<br/><i>"How dare the world be beautiful, when I was so horrifying?"</i> (accompanied by self-hate and self-harm)<br/>To:<br/><i>"We were all monsters and bastards, and w</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6235359174965912563" style="display:none">4.5 rounded up - crazy well written.<br /><br />Seraphina deserves every YA award for which it was nominated. The core objective of the book is to teach young ladies to accept their minds and bodies and grow into natural self-confidence. <br />Seraphina, the heroine of the story, undergoes a huge amount of character development in learning to love herself. She goes from:<br /><i>"How dare the world be beautiful, when I was so horrifying?"</i> (accompanied by self-hate and self-harm)<br />To:<br /><i>"We were all monsters and bastards, and we were all beautiful."</i><br />Seraphina isn't the only one with character growth. Orma and the dragon king learn to cope with human emotions without shutting them off. Prince Lucian Kiggs comes to understand that dragons aren't inherently evil, just different (and accepts his own past in the process).<br />Rachel Hartman gave all her characters, in the foreground and background, journeys with valuable lessons the reader can take away after finishing.<br /><br />I didn't give the audiobook my full attention 100% of the time so I might have missed some aspects of the story, unfortunately.<br /><br />I'm reading Shadow Scale next month. Hopefully it measures up to this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6235359174965912563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_281715257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281715257" />
    <a title="K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2327078-k"><img alt="K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357523905p2/2327078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281715257?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="K." href="/user/show/2327078-k">K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-dys">fantasy-sci-fi-dys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=ok-fine-its-ya">ok-fine-its-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=goosebumps">goosebumps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=this-shelf-is-divine">this-shelf-is-divine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=society-culture-and-politics">society-culture-and-politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=identity-and-psychology">identity-and-psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=hit-me-in-the-heart">hit-me-in-the-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281715257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16403574931994080910"><i>"He released the last chord like a boulder off a trebuchet."</i> It always feels this way when ending a book. There's a weight to the final words, then you let them go and they're gone.<br/><br/>I don't think I've read a young adult book quite like <i>Seraphina</i> before. Rachel Hartman has built for us a world so rich and unique that it is almost dizzying to walk into. Her world is swathed in dark colours depicting a tale of menacing dragons who advocate peace, a stiff but admirably stalwart royal family of Queens</span>
  <span id="freeText16403574931994080910" style="display:none"><i>"He released the last chord like a boulder off a trebuchet."</i> It always feels this way when ending a book. There's a weight to the final words, then you let them go and they're gone.<br /><br />I don't think I've read a young adult book quite like <i>Seraphina</i> before. Rachel Hartman has built for us a world so rich and unique that it is almost dizzying to walk into. Her world is swathed in dark colours depicting a tale of menacing dragons who advocate peace, a stiff but admirably stalwart royal family of Queens and princesses, mothers persecuted, abandoned children, a gang of grotesques, a population of almost-dragons living like scum on the outskirts of humanity, exiled knights, music, love, war, betrayal, identity, lies and truths, a people divided between acceptance and hostility towards the winged-beasts, and finally, those caught in between. <br /><br />The story sweeps you off your feet as a dragon might clamp its talons on your shoulders and whisk you away. It's a story of politics and race, a treaty created between dragons and humans. It has been 40 years since the war and both societies live in relative tolerance -- until a prince's ill-timed murder disturbs this veil of peace, and the animosity, simmering heatedly under the cloak of politeness and adherence to the new law, is given permission to seep out in full force. <br /><br />Seraphina, our protagonist, is a musical protege. She is also half dragon. She is removed, out of necessity, in all ways a young girl coming into her own cannot afford to be ; she layers her clothes to hide her scales as she layers over her heart to protect her loneliness. Seraphina is quite a bundle of maddening sadness but it never feels too heavy because she is also dignified, intelligent, and wants always to do the right thing. Seraphina's sense of alienation, of one who cannot fathom ever being loved, effectively evokes sympathy; a universal sentiment written with care and perception. It is a girl living in the shadows, looking out on all the things she's missing. <i>"Speak more, Seraphina,"</i> they said. <i>"Socialize more."</i> But it was hard for her to open her heart to happiness because with that came the risk of disappointment. But she does, and the path there is poignantly paved. <br /><br />What took me by surprise, but not really considering the impressive writing, is how concrete many of the secondary characters turned out to be. They undergo development. Too many times are these characters treated like caricatures; jesters forfeited for the sake of dramatic enhancement of the lead. Hartman generously allows them their own struggles and triumphs and they are wonderful: a young, impressionable queen-to-be who surpasses expectations; a dragon in human form, guarded but beginning to accept what it is to love; and a bastard prince caught in a battle between history and identity. <br /><br />There's a lot about sacrifice here. There's a lot about many things here, but that in particular struck a chord. Sacrifice in the sense of knowing and understanding where we stand in life and how at times we must give up a part of ourselves for the greater good -- in whatever terms such situations may arise. Also courage; to pull ourselves from our heap of despair and become whole again. Staving off pain when doing something we do not want to but must. And loneliness. The grave acceptance that being alone just comes all too naturally; that you almost would rather be in solitude than let yourself be seen -- worst of all, be wanted. But as Seraphina learns, that is not a way to live and that in fact, when you look close enough, you'll realize you have more than you ever dared believe you did.<br /><br />Hartman's words are exquisite. Her imagination is expansive. Her world is detailed and fascinating. She has created laws, and religion, and a history. She has built architecture, painted landscapes, and constructed streets and alleyways. She has peopled her world with characters of different shades -- from rebels to teachers, musicians to politicians, royalty, knights, outcasts and lovers. <br /><br />Most bizarrely is Hartman's use of her semi-imagined language. I cannot say how many words I had to look up, discovering that the ones I thought were make-believe were in fact real, and ones I simply thought were foreign were fiction. It was both frustrating and marvelous. Her world is so prosperous of information that characters have entire conversations about philosophers we know nothing about. It puts us on the outside, leaving us in confusion over whether to feel left out or in awe. <br /><br />All I have to say is that it was about time Rachel Hartman came along. This was quite extraordinary. My paltry attempt at a review can never stress how much good this has to offer. It is passion, intrigue and adventure; eloquence, excitement, and emotion. It may have lacked action in the way that knowing this is a dragon book might lead you to believe, but it is only the first of the series. Hartman is still holding out.<br /><br />---<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2012/08/seraphina-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An ARC was provided by the publisher. </i><br /><br />---<br /><br />First read: May 2012</span>
  <a data-text-id="16403574931994080910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
