    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_369484870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369484870" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369484870?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375866562" href="/book/show/12394100-seraphina">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-good-it-s-awesome">so-good-it-s-awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369484870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8105397033991499894">"We were all monsters and bastards, and we were all beautiful."<br/><br/>Seraphina Dombegh is an assistant to court musician, Viridius, and is desperately trying to keep a secret that could very well ruin her life. As she works in the court amongst a tenuous peace between humans and dragons, Prince Rufus is violently killed. Slowly, Seraphina is drawn into solving the murder and learning that something rotten is afoot.<br/><br/>What an absolutely delightful reading experience! I thoroughly enjoyed myself while read</span>
  <span id="freeText8105397033991499894" style="display:none">"We were all monsters and bastards, and we were all beautiful."<br /><br />Seraphina Dombegh is an assistant to court musician, Viridius, and is desperately trying to keep a secret that could very well ruin her life. As she works in the court amongst a tenuous peace between humans and dragons, Prince Rufus is violently killed. Slowly, Seraphina is drawn into solving the murder and learning that something rotten is afoot.<br /><br />What an absolutely delightful reading experience! I thoroughly enjoyed myself while reading this. And although there were some bumps that kept this from being a full Five Star read, this is a book that I think fantasy and YA fans will positively enjoy.<br /><br />The absolute best part of the book is the world building. Hartman pulls out all the stops in creating this psuedo-Medieval novel. I've complained numerous times about the flat, unimpressive, unconvincing world building of many a novel, where the author tossed up a few key words but didn't try to flesh out the world, like a college student would toss up a bedsheet onto a rod instead of buying proper curtains. Hartman isn't such an author. The Medieval setting was fresh, new, and inviting; I loved how she developed her own religion complete with a cast of Saints (who were used consistently!). And while I was nervous about the dragons posing as humans (how could such large beasts get into such a small package), somehow, Hartman made it work.<br /><br />And this leads to one of the next best parts: dragons vs humans. To compare the dragon way of thinking to the Star Trek Vulcans would be appropriate. Orma most definitely comes closest to personifying Commander Spock--logical, unemotional, but when something happens to the ones he loves, he goes out of his way to find a solution. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You even see this sort of thing happening in Seraphina. Many times, she seems distant and unemotional...and then you learn she is part-dragon. Somehow, that works for me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Speaking of characters, the cast is filled to the brim with vivid characters. Seraphina is our lead, and while she has her aggravating moments, overall, I liked her. She was active in her own life, curious, gifted; she struggled with her ancestry, with her secret, and with her growing feelings to Kiggs. If there was one problem with her, it was how quickly she decided that she was in love with Kiggs. (Not to say, however, that Seraphina and Kiggs had no chemistry, but I am getting ahead of myself.) Orma was brilliant, as I touched on above; Kiggs was a joy to read. So many male main characters/love interests come across as domineering d-bags, but Kiggs was not that guy. He was abrupt and candid at times, but that is his character. He is allowed to be flawed (who wants to read about perfect characters all the time?).<br /><br />As for Kiggs and Seraphina, minus how quickly Seraphina decides she loves Kiggs, I actually liked them together. They spent time talking and getting to know each other--which is why, when Seraphina decides halfway through the book that she loves Kiggs, I was disappointed. Don't ruin a good couple with insta-love, please!<br /><br />Besides our main couple, there were plenty of other characters to love. Lars, Viridius, Abdo, and my personal favorite, Dame Orka. They were unique and memorable, gifted with their own talents and able to assist Seraphina where needed. And I can't tell you how good it was to see Seraphina in a world with people other than her Love Interest. I get tired of a world filled that seems to hold only a girl and the boy(s) she love(s).<br /><br />However, some of the other characters were a bit...wonky. Glisselda starts out the novel as a ditzy, young princess and suddenly becomes a competent, political-savvy figure by the end of the novel. This change was not well-documented, nor was it clear if Glisselda had been acting the role of the "idiot" in the beginning (perhaps she was, but what made her suddenly accept Seraphina into the role of confidante?). While I didn't much care for Glisselda either way in the beginning, I did like how she became a good, solid leader in the end and a friend to Seraphina (another thing I hate is how few female friends a female protagonist will have, as if they are competition or a distraction to our MC).<br /><br />Seraphina's dad and her stepmother/siblings were other characters that I was surprised to see so little of. Claude is spoken of quite frequently, but he appears maybe a total of twice in the novel. I know Seraphina doesn't have the greatest of relationships with him, but I found it slightly odd, as they did both work in the castle. As for the stepmother/stepsiblings, I was a bit surprised at this descriptor found in the glossary:<br /><br /><blockquote><b>Anne-Marie</b>-- Phina's not-so-wicked stepmother<br /><br /><b>Tessie, Jeanne, Paul, and Nedward</b>-- the moderately wicked stepsibilings</blockquote><br /><br />Anne-Marie, like Claude, barely appears in the novel, but at least, she exemplifies the description. The stepsiblings, however, are said to be "moderately wicked", but not once do they do anything "moderately wicked". They are actually really polite to their older sibling, in the one scene we see them. Is this glossary entry just supposed to be joking? Given the other entries, such as Prince Lucian's, I almost think this is the case:<br /><br /><blockquote><b>Prince Lucian Kiggs</b>-- Princess Laurel's embarrassing bastard, fiance of Princess Glisselda, Captain of the Queen's Guard, possessor of too many descriptors</blockquote><br /><br />And let me take the chance now to say: THANK YOU, RACHEL HARTMAN, FOR THE GLOSSARY!! I've read far too many novels lately with a bunch of new people, terms, locations, etc. and have been completely lost.<br /><br />As for the story, the novel opens very slowly. VERY SLOWLY. A lot of pages are spent building up this world and the surroundings before launching into the main plot. Also, the beginning is a bit rough. I wish I could be more specific, but all I can say is that the first 20 pages or so were a bit challenging to get through. After that point, the book seems to hit its stride, and the flow is a lot better. And once the plot does eventually kick into gear, it is very good. It is unique, our main character, Seraphina, actually acts upon her life (instead of having others make decisions for her and just "float" through the story), and the mystery did have me stumped (for a bit). And I liked how the story concludes: a nice ending, completing this book, but definitely room to continue the story.<br /><br />And this is definitely a series I will be following. Sure, there were missteps and I'm sure there are gonna be a lot of people who won't want to wade through the world-building at the beginning before the story kicks into gear, but I enjoyed myself. I liked the world, the characters, and the story and am a bit sad that I'm going to have to wait a year or so for book 2. Recommended for fans of fantasy and dragons and heroines that don't need a boy toy to do all their dirty work.<br /><br /><b>UPDATE</b><br /><br />After careful consideration, I've decided to leave this series right here. Some initial reviews indicated story directions that aren't my thing, but also, I've been moving away from the Young Adult genre for months. I don't even know that Today Me would like this book - I've changed so much, read more books, etc.<br /><br />That said, my Old Self who read numerous different YA DID like this book; hence, I won't be removing this review or updating the review itself unless or until I reread the book.<br /><br />Dialogue/Sexual Situations/Violence:<br />Very tame. Lucian is called a "b*****d" but in the familial sense. Other curses are invented slang or mild expletives ("da**", "he**").<br />One character's backstory includes his mother sleeping with a dragon. Lucian and Seraphina exchange a few kisses, but nothing more. The sexuality of a few characters is mentioned, but only briefly and not in graphic detail.<br />The story opens with the murder of Prince Rufus, whose head was apparently bit off. A group of men beat up a saar. Seraphina's old teacher held her over a balcony and threatened to kill her. Otherwise, fairly mild.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8105397033991499894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1138705430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138705430" />
    <a title="Denisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse"><img alt="Denisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606102662p2/8759700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138705430?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisse" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse">Denisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138705430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5315478912509064339"><b>Buddy Read 02/04/2015 with the Emma's Tea Party</b> aka my favorite group ever. <s>I'll bring the tequila, shhh!</s><br/><br/><b>Read for the 2015 Reading Challenge: #7 A book with non-human characters</b><br/><br/><b>3.5</b> Seraphina is a good fantasy book. With a winning mix of fantasy , politics and romance that we have read a lot already. Its biggest mistake is following every single fantasy rule and adding very little extra details. But is <b>definitely worth reading for any fantasy lover.</b> Not remarkable, but enjoyable. <br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Our survival</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText5315478912509064339" style="display:none"><b>Buddy Read 02/04/2015 with the Emma's Tea Party</b> aka my favorite group ever. <s>I'll bring the tequila, shhh!</s><br /><br /><b>Read for the 2015 Reading Challenge: #7 A book with non-human characters</b><br /><br /><b>3.5</b> Seraphina is a good fantasy book. With a winning mix of fantasy , politics and romance that we have read a lot already. Its biggest mistake is following every single fantasy rule and adding very little extra details. But is <b>definitely worth reading for any fantasy lover.</b> Not remarkable, but enjoyable. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Our survival depends not on being superior but on being sufficiently interesting."</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />Es muy raro encontrarte joyas de fantasia juvenil. <b>Seraphina tenia todas las de ganar, desgraciadamente hubo muchos hilos flojos y sus puntos fuertes son tramas que hemos visto ya bastantes veces en mil fantasías distintas.</b> Y aunque Seraphina sigue muy bien las "reglas" no se atreve a desviarse mucho y por ende, no sobresale del genero para nada, en mi opinión. <br /><br />Ademas que tarda bastantito en arrancar, y lo mejor del libro no sucede hasta después de la segunda mitad, lo cual puede ser frustrante para muchos. <br /><br />Los personajes son todos muy buenos, pero mi opinión es la misma, están la clásica protagonista que es diferente y debe esconder su diferencia. El interés amoroso de la realeza que tiene un deber, pero empieza a enamorarse, pero sigue teniendo un deber. La amiga de la realeza medio mensa pero al final no tanto. La figura sabia. El antagonista malo-muy-malo. Y un montón de otros personajes que no conocemos bien por el simple hecho de agregar misterio. Y aunque todos son buenos personajes, ninguno llega a brillar demasiado porque todos siguen las "reglas" de los típicos personajes de fantasía. Orma y Glisselda son mis favoritos.<br /><br /><b>La trama es buena, pero predecible desde la mitad del libro.</b> Ademas que al inicio parece que seguirá una dirección y para la mitad parece que la autora cambia de opinión y no se digna a cambiar cosas del inicio. <b>El dialogo bueno pero nada especial. La historia de amor bien manejada pero cliche, </b>y sale de -literalmente hablando- ninguna parte <s>what?</s><br /><br />Ya me estoy dando a entender con lo que dije antes de <i>"no sobresale del genero para nada"</i>? y eso que yo no leo TAAAAAANTO fantasía como mucha otra gente. <br /><br />A pesar de eso, hay descripciones muy buenas. Y la forma de escribir de la autora es muy linda y eso ayuda mucho a un fantasy. Y la visión que tiene la autora sobre los dragones y sus diferencias con los humanos es muy interesante. Desgraciadamente eso de <i>"somos dragones y tenemos la habilidad de transformarnos a forma humana y por eso ahora hay paz"</i> se me hace algo muy sencillo que elimina muchos posibles problemas interesantes a que fueran viles bestias-dragones y humanos conviviendo realmente. <br /><br />Recomendado si te gusta el genero. No esperes nada mind-blowing, porque no lo vas a encontrar. Pero es una lectura entretenida con ciertos detalles interesantes y una formula con elementos típicos ganadores.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5315478912509064339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EO3X3iNdwx0YlALEjNn7FTn1A0i+yr3BvzCTGmK/gmcqy74MmAMKdb+/tqV7LPHK76rkgHBHM6bkTtWrr/xw/Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TiQbpCGC1RPZBWp6hytC8zLRQBl3XUehbjo16s7M4wp0AnJ2mtwce34u3htw3kgs5I6n0bnQycY1RHNbA48RkA==')})
  }

Here are some things that are already being said about <i>Seraphina</i> by some fabulous authors:<br/><br/>“A book worth hoarding, as glittering and silver-bright as dragon scales, with a heroine who insists on carving herself a place in your mind.” — Naomi Novik, New York Times</span>
  <span id="freeText12542766018810703141" style="display:none">Rachel Hartman lives and writes in Vancouver, BC.<br /><br />Her first YA fantasy novel, <i>Seraphina</i>, was published by Random House on July 10th, 2012. Here are some things that are already being said about <i>Seraphina</i> by some fabulous authors:<br /><br />“A book worth hoarding, as glittering and silver-bright as dragon scales, with a heroine who insists on carving herself a place in your mind.” — Naomi Novik, New York Times bestselling author of the Temeraire series.<br /><br />“Seraphina is strong, complex, talented — she makes mistakes and struggles to trust, with good reason, and she fights to survive in a world that would tear her apart. I love this book!” — Tamora Pierce, New York Times bestselling author.<br /><br />“Just when you thought there was nothing new to say about dragons, it turns out there is, and plenty! Rachel Hartman’s rich invention never fails to impress — and to convince. It’s smart and funny and original, and has characters I will follow to the ends of the earth.” — Ellen Kushner, World Fantasy Award-winning author.</span>
